A \u2243 4\u03c3 dust detection is seen at 1.2mm as part of the ALMA Lensing Cluster Survey (ALCS), an on-going ALMA Large programme, and the redshift is secured via [C II] 158 \u03bcm emission described in a companion paper. In addition, spectroscopic follow-up with GMOS/Gemini-North shows a break in the galaxy's spectrum, consistent with the Lyman break at that redshift. We use a detailed mass model of the cluster and infer a magnification \u03bc \u2273 30 for the most magnified image of this galaxy, which provides an unprecedented opportunity to probe the physical properties of a sub-luminous galaxy at the end of cosmic reionization. Based on the spectral energy distribution, we infer lensing-corrected stellar and dust masses of $\\rm {2.9^{+11.5}_{-2.3}\\times 10^9}$ and $\\rm {4.8^{+4.5}_{-3.4}\\times 10^6}$$\\rm {M_{\\odot }}$, respectively, a star formation rate of $\\rm {9.7^{+22.0}_{-6.6} \\, M_{\\odot } \\, yr^{-1}}$, an intrinsic size of $\\rm {0.54^{+0.26}_{-0.14}}$ kpc, and a luminosity-weighted age of 200 \u00b1 100 Myr. Strikingly, the dust production rate in this relatively young galaxy appears to be larger than that observed for equivalent, lower redshift sources. We discuss if this implies that early supernovae are more efficient dust producers and the consequences for using dust mass as a probe of earlier star formation.", "doi": "10.1093/mnras/stab191", </div>\r\n</div>\r\n<input id=\"hfEnableOupOnlineProductsFeatures\" name=\"hfEnableOupOnlineProductsFeatures\" type=\"hidden\" value=\"False\" />\r\n\r\n<input id=\"routename\" name=\"RouteName\" type=\"hidden\" value=\"mnras\" /> \r\n    </div>\r\n\r\n                    </div>\r\n                </div>\r\n            </div>\r\n            <div id=\"ContentTab\" class=\"content active\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\r\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=266960814 id=\"266960814\" class=\"abstract-title js-splitscreen-abstract-title\" >ABSTRACT</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">We report the discovery of an intrinsically faint, quintuply-imaged, dusty galaxy MACS0600-z6 at a redshift <em>z</em> = 6.07 viewed through the cluster MACSJ0600.1\u20132008 (<em>z</em> = 0.46). A \u2243 4\u03c3 dust detection is seen at 1.2mm as part of the ALMA Lensing Cluster Survey (ALCS), an on-going ALMA Large programme, and the redshift is secured via [C\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] 158 <em>\u03bc</em>m emission described in a companion paper. In addition, spectroscopic follow-up with GMOS/Gemini-North shows a break in the galaxy\u2019s spectrum, consistent with the Lyman break at that redshift. We use a detailed mass model of the cluster and infer a magnification \u03bc \u2273 30 for the most magnified image of this galaxy, which provides an unprecedented opportunity to probe the physical properties of a sub-luminous galaxy at the end of cosmic reionization. Based on the spectral energy distribution, we infer lensing-corrected stellar and dust masses of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm {2.9^{+11.5}_{-2.3}\\times 10^9}$|</span> and <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm {4.8^{+4.5}_{-3.4}\\times 10^6}$|</span><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm {M_{\\odot }}$|\u2060</span>, respectively, a star formation rate of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm {9.7^{+22.0}_{-6.6} \\, M_{\\odot } \\, yr^{-1}}$|\u2060</span>, an intrinsic size of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm {0.54^{+0.26}_{-0.14}}$|</span> kpc, and a luminosity-weighted age of 200\u00a0\u00b1\u00a0100\u00a0Myr. Strikingly, the dust production rate in this relatively young galaxy appears to be larger than that observed for equivalent, lower redshift sources. We discuss if this implies that early supernovae are more efficient dust producers and the consequences for using dust mass as a probe of earlier star formation.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix at-ArticleMetadata\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: evolution&quot;\">galaxies: evolution</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: formation&quot;\">galaxies: formation</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: high-redshift&quot;\">galaxies: high-redshift</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=266960816 id=\"266960816\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Understanding the process of cosmic reionization, during which intergalactic hydrogen transforms from a neutral to an ionized state in less than a billion years, represents a major challenge in extragalactic astronomy and cosmology. Although star-forming galaxies are considered to be the primary ionizing sources, those which can be directly observed during the reionization era appear to be insufficient in number given their likely ionization output (e.g. Robertson et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib60\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib60\" data-open=\"bib60\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). As a consequence, it is popular to appeal to contributions from a larger number of sub-luminous sources, which can only be partially probed via current deep surveys (e.g. Bouwens et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Livermore, Finkelstein &amp; Lotz <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib50\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib50\" data-open=\"bib50\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>; Bhatawdekar et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>; Kikuchihara et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>). With current facilities, the only way to characterize the physical properties of this sub-luminous population is to use the magnification afforded by gravitational lensing (for a review see Kneib &amp; Natarajan <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>). Although several surveys have harnessed the lensing power of foreground clusters, such as the Cluster Lensing And Supernova survey with Hubble (CLASH; Postman et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib58\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib58\" data-open=\"bib58\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), the <em>Hubble</em> Frontier Fields (Lotz et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib51\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib51\" data-open=\"bib51\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) and most recently REionization LensIng Cluster Survey (RELICS; Coe et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>), the effective surface area explored for the most highly magnified background sources remains small. As a consequence, very few high-redshift sources (<em>z</em> \u2265 6) with magnifications \u03bc \u2265 10 have so far been found (e.g. Coe et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Salmon et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib61\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib61\" data-open=\"bib61\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Of particular interest in physical studies of galaxies in the reionization era is their dust content. Although dust can obscure the ionizing radiation and lead to underestimates of properties such as star formation rate and ionizing capability, dust masses have been proposed as a potential way forward in estimating the earlier star formation histories and hence ages of early galaxies (Laporte et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib48\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib48\" data-open=\"bib48\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017b</a>; Katz et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib38\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib38\" data-open=\"bib38\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>). It is typically assumed that dust at early times is largely produced in core-collapse supernovae with a production rate similar to that observed in local events (&lt;0.2\u00a0M<sub>\u2299</sub> per event, e.g. Indebetouw et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib34\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib34\" data-open=\"bib34\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). However, little is known about dust production rates at early times and thus correlating dust properties of early galaxies over the full range of stellar masses with stellar ages inferred independently from spectral energy distributions (SEDs) would be highly valuable. To date. there are very few convincing dust detections beyond <em>z</em> \u2243 6 (e.g. Capak et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Watson et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib69\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib69\" data-open=\"bib69\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Brada\u010d et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>; Laporte et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib48\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib48\" data-open=\"bib48\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017b</a>; Marrone et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib52\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib52\" data-open=\"bib52\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>; Hashimoto et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib32\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib32\" data-open=\"bib32\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>; Tamura et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib68\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib68\" data-open=\"bib68\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>) and none for galaxies with UV magnitude <em>M</em><sub>uv</sub> &gt; \u221218</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The ALMA Lensing Cluster Survey (ALCS; PI: K. Kohno) is motivated by multiple goals including probing the dust properties of strongly lensed galaxies near the end of the epoch of reionization. The programme has observed 33 clusters (5 from the Frontier Fields survey, 12 from CLASH and 16 from RELICS) in ALMA band-6 (\u03bb \u223c 1.2mm) to reach a 5\u03c3 lensing-corrected rms of \u22640.1 mJy over 16 arcmin<sup>2</sup> (or 0.01 mJy over the 0.5 arcmin<sup>2</sup> for the highest magnification regions). In this paper, we report the discovery of dust-emission from a multiply-imaged lensed system MACS0600-z6 at <em>z</em> = 6.07 behind one of the ALCS clusters, MACSJ0600.1-2008 (Ebeling, Edge &amp; Henry <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>). In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">2</a>, we describe the relevant observational data and the photometry of the lensed source. Based on three mass models described in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">3</a>, we identify five multiple images for this system, infer a total magnification of \u03bc \u2273 30 for the most magnified arc. Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">4</a> presents spectroscopic follow-up with Gemini-North of several images, and we discuss the physical properties of this system in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">5</a>. Throughout this paper, we assume <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${H_0=70 \\, \\mathrm{km\\, s^{-1}\\, Mpc}^{-1}}$|\u2060</span>, \u03a9<sub>m</sub> = 0.3, and \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub> = 0.7. All magnitudes are in AB system (Oke &amp; Gunn <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib55\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib55\" data-open=\"bib55\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1983</a>).</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=266960820 id=\"266960820\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 OBSERVATION AND DATA ANALYSIS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The cluster MACSJ0600.1-2008 (<em>z</em> = 0.46) was observed as part of the ALMA Lensing Cluster Survey (ID: 2018.1.00035.L; P.I. Kohno, K.) in band 6 frequency in January 2019 with a total exposure time of 3.3 h. The data was reduced using the ALMA pipeline (v. 5.6.1-8) with a natural weighting. A 2\u00a0arcsec <em>uv</em>-taper was used to maximize the detection of faint sources. The final beam size is 2.\u200921\u00a0arcsec\u00a0\u00d7\u00a01.99\u00a0arcsec and the rms on the reduced mosaic is 80 <em>\u03bc</em>Jy\u2009beam<sup>\u22121</sup>. 13 sources with a signal-to-noise ratio (SNR) \u2265 4 were identified including one at RA = 06:00:09.143 and Dec. = \u221220:08:26.579 with an elongated half-light radius of 1.3\u00a0arcsec. By extracting the flux on a line-free image at 1.2\u00a0mm using the CASA <em>imfit</em> task, the peak flux is <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm {S^{peak}_{1.2\\, mm}}$|</span> = 366\u00a0\u00b1\u00a062 <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm {\\mu Jy\\, beam^{-1}}$|</span> and the integrated flux is <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm {S^{int}_{1.2mm}}$|</span> = 484\u00a0\u00b1\u00a0135 <em>\u03bc</em>Jy on an emission line subtracted image.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">A search for an ultraviolet (UV) rest-frame counterpart for this source was undertaken on deep <em>HST</em> images from the RELICS survey with a search radius of 2\u00a0arcsec. The data reduction of this data set is described in Coe et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>). Photometric catalogues were built using version 2.19.5 of <em>SE\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">xtractor</span></em> Bertin &amp; Arnouts (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1996</a>) in dual image mode on psf matched images. The extraction parameters were defined to maximize the detection of faint objects (DETECT_THRESH = 2\u03c3; ANALYSIS_THRESH = 2\u03c3; DETECT_MINAREA = 5 px) on a detection picture composed by the sum of all WFC3 images. The final catalogue contains 25200 detections. To estimate the depth of each image, we masked the bright sources and measured the rms in hundreds non-overlapping 0.4\u00a0arcsec radius aperture. Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> summarizes the data properties. Two overlapping sources were detected 0<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${_{.}^{\\prime\\prime}}$|</span>\u20094 South of the ALMA detection (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>): a point source (referred to hereafter as \u2018foreground\u2019) and a background arc-like source (referred to as MACS0600-z6, whose discovery multiple image is denoted MACS0600-arc, see below for more details). The foreground source was identified in the public RELICS catalogue (Salmon et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib62\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib62\" data-open=\"bib62\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>) and assigned a photometric redshift of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm {z_{phot}}$|</span> = 0.82<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$^{+0.28}_{-0.40}$|\u2060</span>. The multiple image MACS0600-arc is absent from that pipeline-generated catalogue, most likely because of its faintness and elongated shape.</p>                        <a id=\"266960823\" scrollto-destination=\"266960823\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/505/4/10.1093_mnras_stab191/1/m_stab191fig1.jpeg?Expires=1639262618&amp;Signature=L1hWjJFew6CjMa1FV0sRN6PdaVJrwlbIBhhZPL4lRfUKppaIfVN6Oh-dkrFjdzYhD2Uxr-cz8LOk~t2R07T3~arRv8OZRTNKukd1QXgT-2O7q3Ma6A7oUz61KsgtFy3qlagY7DVBFXP64fOxOL0u6kqejC9HOJQT1sIfUxzbVQcYMrBcT3C-Sc1YR7s0~bX0yEGc2IBPo9uxhdvSw7G1o3ZDgwA0K6aGjaJusWQwQyyNdB0cxGaUlmhhlkNJE2UYhN0e8VvRfidb7TUdtMALxTtQNSbKDLAc5iXWnRJwSzc61A~HvGf-v191UEsJWACw8b4SS5CQRNYjwltkU9Ai0g__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Thumbnail images of MACS0600-arc comprising images from ACS/HST (F435W, F606W, F814W), WFC3-IR/HST (F105W, F125W, F140W and F160W), HAWK-I/VLT(Ks), IRAC/Spitzer (3.6 and 4.5 \u03bcm), and ALMA (Band 6). class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/266960824\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Noting the overlapping foreground object, in order to extract the photometry of MACS0600-arc we model each source with a Sersic profile using <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> (Peng et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib57\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib57\" data-open=\"bib57\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>) on the WFC3-NIR and IRAC images, which accounts for PSF difference between <em>HST</em>, VLT, and <em>Spitzer</em>. Error bars are measured on the residual image in a 0.\u20094\u00a0arcsec radius circle. We tested our method on the ACS data where only the foreground source is detected and compared the <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> photometry with that derived using the standard MAG_AUTO photometry in single image mode with SE\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">xtractor</span> (Bertin &amp; Arnouts <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1996</a>). In F606W, our extracted photometry (<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">\u2060|$\\rm {m_{F606W}^{GALFIT} = 26.55\\pm 0.35}$|\u2060</span>) is in excellent agreement with the SE\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">xtractor</span> photometry (<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">\u2060|$\\rm {m_{F606W}^{SExtractor} = 26.72\\pm 0.08}$|\u2060</span>). A similar conclusion is seen for the F814W image.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">To increase the wavelength coverage, we searched for deep public data at longer wavelength. Using the ESO archive, we found a deep Ks exposure carried out with HAWKI/VLT (ID: 0100.A-785; P.I.: A. Edge) reaching a 2\u03c3 depth in 1.2\u00a0arcsec radius aperture of 24.4. We also searched in the <em>Spitzer</em> archive for deep IRAC 3.6 and 4.5 <em>\u03bc</em>m exposures. This cluster was part of two observing programs (ID: 90218; P.I.: E. Egami and ID: 12005, P.I. : M. Bradac), we combined all exposures and measured the depth in a 1.2\u00a0arcsec radius aperture distributed over the field of view. We present the final photometry in Table <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"266960827\" scrollto-destination=\"266960827\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl2\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl2\" data-id=\"tbl2\"><span class=\"label\">Table 2.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Photometry of the multiple images of this <em>z</em> \u2265 6 system. Upper photometric limits on the ACS and WFC3 data were estimated in a 0.4\u00a0arcsec radius aperture, on HAWK-I data in a 0.8\u00a0arcsec radius aperture (taking into account the seeing of the data), and in a 1.2\u00a0arcsec radius aperture for IRAC images. For the photometric extraction of z6.3a and z6.3b, we used GALFIT on ACS and WFC3 images assuming a Sersic profile for both. On the IRAC data, where the separation is not clearly resolved, we used the flux ratio observed at 1.6\u2009<em>\u03bc</em>m to separate the contribution of each source.</p></div> </div><div For the photometric extraction of z6.3a and z6.3b, we used GALFIT on ACS and WFC3 images assuming a Sersic profile for both. On the IRAC data, where the separation is not clearly resolved, we used the flux ratio observed at 1.6\u2009<em>\u03bc</em>m to separate the contribution of each source.</p></div> </div><div content-id=\"tblfn1\" class=\"footnote\"><span class=\"fn\"><p class=\"chapter-para\"><em><sup>a</sup></em>Spectroscopically confirmed at <em>z</em> = 6.07 (see Fujimoto et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2021</a>).</p></span></div><span id=\"fn-tblfn2\"></span><div content-id=\"tblfn2\" class=\"footnote\"><span class=\"fn\"><p class=\"chapter-para\"><em><sup>b</sup></em>Candidates for the fifth image of this system. The absence of WFC3 data at the expected position makes difficult the clear identification of the image.</p></span></div></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/266960827\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">We determine the photometric redshift of the foreground source from a template-based SED-fitting method with <span class=\"small-caps\">Hyperz</span> (Bolzonella, Miralles &amp; Pell\u00f3 <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>). We used the standard list of templates including evolutionary SEDs with Chabrier IMF (Chabrier <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>) and solar metallicity from Bruzual &amp; Charlot (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>), empirical SEDs built by Coleman, Wu &amp; Weedman (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1980</a>) and two starburst galaxies from Kinney et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib41\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib41\" data-open=\"bib41\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1996</a>). We then searched for a solution between 0 &lt; <em>z</em> &lt; 8, with an extinction range <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm {0.0 \\lt {\\it A}_v \\lt 3.0}$|</span> mag assuming a Calzetti reddening law (Calzetti et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>). The colour of the foreground source is similar to the colour of cluster members, we therefore allow a redshift range of <em>z</em> \u2208 [0.0:3.0]. The best SED-fit for the foreground source is obtained at <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm {z_{phot} = 0.57^{+0.14}_{-0.17}}$|</span> and modest reddening (<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">\u2060|$\\rm {A_v}$|</span> = 1.5\u00a0mag). Allowing a larger redshift range, the MACS0600-arc data provide a solution at <em>z</em><sub>photo</sub> = <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$6.68^{+0.24}_{-0.67}$|</span> with an extinction <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm {A_v}$|</span> = 0.5\u00a0mag, broadly consistent with the spectroscopic value (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>).</p>                        <a id=\"266960829\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab191fig2.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">SED of MACS0600-z6 showing the best fit from MAGPHYS and the best physical properties corrected for magnification.</p></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=266960830 id=\"266960830\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 LENS MODELS AND MULTIPLE IMAGES</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The elongated shape of the prominent <em>z</em> \u223c 6 arc supports the suggestion of a strongly lensed source. To determine the lensing configuration and hence the intrinsic properties of this source and the associated uncertainties, we have utilized several different lens models from within the ALCS team. These models exploit spectroscopic observations of MACS0600 using the MUSE integral field unit spectrograph (ID 0100.A-0792; PI: Edge) and the photometric redshift catalogue from RELICS. More details on the lens modelling of MACS0600 will be given in a separate paper, and here we provide only a brief summary. For convenience in this section, we drop the prefix MACS0600 in describing the multiple images.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The three models used here are produced using <span class=\"small-caps\">glafic</span> (Oguri <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib54\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib54\" data-open=\"bib54\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>), <span class=\"small-caps\">Lenstool</span> (Jullo et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>), and Light-Traces-Mass (LTM; Zitrin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib70\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib70\" data-open=\"bib70\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). The first two models can be regarded as parametric in the sense that both the galaxies and their dark matter haloes are described using independent analytic forms (e.g. combinations of pseudo-isothermal elliptical mass distributions) and adopt empirical scaling relations for cluster members. The LTM method is similar, but here the dark matter is assumed to follow the light distribution and thus is modelled as a smoothed version of the luminosity-weighted galaxy distribution. The parametric modelling of MACS0600 typically included three to four dark matter haloes and, whereas for the LTM models, the masses of several bright cluster members were modeled independently. All models are minimized using available multiple image constraints to find the best-fitting solution and its associated errors. Four modellers (MO, JR, GC, AZ) voted on the choice of multiply imaged systems which, besides the <em>z</em> \u223c 6 system, included nine other systems considered as secure. Five of these have a spectroscopic redshift from MUSE (spanning the redshift range <em>z</em> \u223c 1.5 to <em>z</em> \u223c 5.5). All three models indicate that the source MACS0600-z6 is quintuply imaged with the discovery arc (images z6.1 and z6.2) being a pair of multiple images that merge across the critical curve; an additional counter image inside the tangential critical curves (z6.3); a radial image (z6.4); and a fifth image on the other side of the cluster to the west (z6.5). The stamps of the five images are shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>, and the configuration derived from the LTM model for example, including all five multiple images, is shown on a <em>HST</em> image of the cluster in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>. To confirm the reliability of this system, we first check that the colours are similar for the four images within the error bars. We only include one of the fifth image candidates in this analysis (z6.5c) because <em>HST</em> coverage is missing for the other two. Colours measured on WFC3 images are similar with averaged values of F125W-F160W = 0.32\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.15. Another relevant feature that should be conserved by lensing is the surface brightness. We estimated the surface brightness of the four images using the extracted magnitude from GALFIT for the arc and z6.3a,b and from our SE\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">xtractor</span> catalogues for the remaining objects using the MAG_AUTO and the isophotal area. All images have consistent surface brightness in the WFC3 images (e.g. the averaged value on F160W is 21.9\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.3) reinforcing the multiple images system hypothesis.</p>                        <a id=\"266960833\" scrollto-destination=\"266960833\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/505/4/10.1093_mnras_stab191/1/m_stab191fig3.jpeg?Expires=1639262618&amp;Signature=uzRXPWluA-aVzSl0eWEAvmnnkD1R0Is0U0ZUNwZGIufnTzmmp~54wgXSfSwG~0yKdk28xdNODaenIt3Xk0IoV~W2jy7XNfc5Xa7sKxn~c5DbQjA5aSlqCrGSriNFYd3W5HIVByRxwmeD0cWkxuQFbQhVm0BTYqd2wnbzWBkBC1MJfd-FxwWDaR9X8sKFjlA7p0u1jQxr8UCVZyNkBLd1E-OZbe4TVeZG4X5JNhrOun4t4vvq5OhLwPOD-rKRxSDt2kwq5SqttIUZavhTwtnJSlgHJS8PhaxGbPTwEAS7hrVGMEo7yZLT-98mv563MsGNCi36LzHYKICnWBrVb3nyUA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Thumbnail images of all images of the quintuply lensed galaxy presented in this paper. MACS0600-z6.1 and MACS0600-z6.2 (top left) are a merging pair crossing the critical line, and seen on HST images as an elongated arc and referred in the text as MACS0600-arc. MACS0600-z6.3 comprises a bright object (z6.3a) and a fainter, fuzzy part (z6.3b), which is the quintuply imaged part as indicated by the lens models, and on which the line emission seems to be concentrated. ALMA contours are overplotted on the arc stamp from 3\u03c3 and from 2\u03c3 for z6.3b.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab191fig4.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/266960834/stab191fig4.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab191fig4.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"266960834\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/505/4/10.1093_mnras_stab191/1/stab191fig4.jpeg?Expires=1639262618&Signature=e571J40Pq4mF6UuaXEp6hggVZxBLG8ZjrV26-cD-hayogbjgi0OUy60h9O3-Gg~3FD357LP3sO~74hp9KtuF2gXHKXB9CCR9aaQF0SkUhYkVVJM4amJAfWuzv498PfLSNYuHT7xP-3DfJ0C9TGs5yeVdl3rT0w3VG24BIfguYPnxmncSDzm0ltPr7ZMI~KL3ckS9hISxa5v4uWCGLyPsDqTK~sfy2HhHOuMBzVlKblC5SwcIE~TeLCiM~08cdRANy-aYemQHfeydGxfeCUaQPqkikU4kO7Vy1H71gZxhFtp-Lir9XL0EVLo6c52ldGce2MAQZyL5D3KZL~KnbX3ORA__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=266960834&ar=6122579&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab191fig4.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\"><em>Right</em>: Position of the five images of MACS0600-z6 superimposed on a colour <em>HST</em> image (F435W \u2013 blue; F814W \u2013 green; F160W \u2013 red). The white contours from the LTM model are overplotted. <em>Left</em>: Labelled F160W stamps of four multiple images. MACS0600-z6.1 and MACS0600-z6.2 (top left) are a merging pair crossing the critical line, and seen on <em>HST</em> images as an elongated arc and referred in the text as MACS0600-arc. MACS0600-z6.3 comprises a bright object (z6.3a) and a fainter, fuzzy part (z6.3b), which is the quintuply imaged part as indicated by the lens models, and on which the line emission seems to be concentrated. ALMA contours are overplotted on the arc stamp from 3\u03c3 and from 2\u03c3 for z6.3b.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">In addition to the detected arc, two out of the three other predicted images, z6.3 and radial image z6.4, were easily identified in both the <em>HST</em> and ALMA data. These images lie within <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\lt 0{_{.}^{\\prime\\prime}} \\, 4$|</span> of their predicted locations and have photometric redshifts similar to that estimated for MACS0600-arc. In the <em>HST</em> data, image z6.3 consists of a bright \u2018bulge\u2019 referred to here as z6.3a and an additional faint component z6.3b which, according to the three lens models, is likely the multiply imaged counterpart of the arc, and on which the ALMA signal is centred. It is unclear whether image z6.3a is truly part of the lensed source despite not being quintuply imaged as well, and \u2013 while we acknowledge the possibility that z6.3a may be related \u2013 we consider only z6.3b a genuine multiple image of this system. In the ALMA data, z6.3b also shows a faint dust detection with an S/N \u223c 3.5 (<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">\u2060|$\\rm {f_{peak} = 226\\pm 63 \\, \\mu Jy\\, beam^{-1}}$|</span> as measured with imfit). The 1.2 mm flux ratio between 1.3b and the arc is 0.62<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$^{+0.33}_{-0.24}$|</span> in excellent agreement with ratios observed in the near-infrared and with the predicted lens-model magnifications (see below). [C\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]158\u2009<em>\u03bc</em>m emission lines at <em>z</em> = 6.07 are detected in all images of this system that are covered by ALMA\u2019s FOV: the arc, z6.3b, and z6.4, strengthening further the adopted lensing configuration, again with line ratios that commensurate with the expectations from the lens models. More extensive details on these detections are given in a companion paper (Fujimoto et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2021</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">While all models reassuringly agree on the positions of the five multiple images, there is larger scatter (\u223c12\u00a0arcsec) in the predicted location of the fifth image, z6.5. The <span class=\"small-caps\">glafic</span> and <span class=\"small-caps\">ltm</span> models predict image z6.5 lies outside the region covered by WFC3 data, making its identification more challenging, and two objects undetected on the ACS images but seen on the HAWK-I data are considered as potential candidates (z6.5a and z6.5b). The <span class=\"small-caps\">Lenstool</span> model predicts the fifth image within the WFC3 field, and one clear dropout is identified as a potential candidate using the ACS, WFC3, and HAWK-I data (MACS0600-z6.5c).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Magnification factors <em>\u03bc</em> for the five images were estimated as follows. The two parametric models (<span class=\"small-caps\">Lenstool</span> and <span class=\"small-caps\">glafic</span>) extracted values by first planting a compact source in the expected position, and adjusting its exact position with respect to the critical curves to match the observed [C\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] 158 <em>\u03bc</em>m line flux ratio. The LTM magnification values were derived in a slightly different manner: here the source was not planted in the source plane but formed there by directly delensing the arc, and the magnification of the arc was then extracted by comparing the model\u2019s prediction for the three other multiple image sizes with their absolute magnification values. The magnification for the five images from the <span class=\"small-caps\">glafic</span> model is \u03bc \u223c 33 for the arc, \u03bc \u223c 35 for z6.3, \u03bc \u223c 5.7 for z6.4, and \u03bc \u223c 14 for z6.5. The <span class=\"small-caps\">Lenstool</span> model yields \u03bc \u223c 22.1 for the arc, \u03bc \u223c 14 for z6.3, \u03bc \u223c 2.1 for z6.4, and \u03bc \u223c 2.9 for z6.5. The <span class=\"small-caps\">ltm</span> model magnifications are \u03bc \u223c 31.2 for the arc, \u03bc \u223c 13.5 for z6.3, \u03bc \u223c 2.1 for z6.4, and \u03bc \u223c 3.8 for z6.5. We note that the magnifications for the arc are likely lower limits. If the magnification for the arc is instead estimated by directly averaging the magnification next to the critical curves, or alternatively by comparing the area of the arc to its delensed size, values around \u03bc \u223c 150\u2013200 are obtained, although such estimates are typically more uncertain.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We also take benefit from the detection of the dust continuum in two of the multiple images (z6.3 and the arc) to estimate the physical offset between the FIR continuum and the UV continuum. The position of the UV continuum was estimated on the F160W image using the centroid of the counterpart. In the image plan, we measured an observed offset of 0.24 and 0.35\u00a0arcsec, respectively, for z6.3b and the arc. Accounting for the magnification, we estimate a physical offset of &lt;0.4\u00a0kpc.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=266960839 id=\"266960839\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 SPECTROSCOPIC FOLLOW-UP</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The detection of an emission line within the ALMA band 6 datacube suggests a redshift <em>z</em><sub>spec</sub> = 6.07, assuming the line is [C\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]158\u2009<em>\u03bc</em>m (Fujimoto et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2021</a>). However, with only one line detected, a low/intermediate redshift interloper cannot be excluded. The relatively shallow MUSE data used to constrain the mass models did not show any features for the multiple-images of this system. Therefore, we conducted a spectroscopic follow-up campaign with the Gemini Multi-Object Spectrograph (GMOS; Hook et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib33\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib33\" data-open=\"bib33\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>) installed on Gemini-North on three images of the system, namely MACS0600-arc, MACS0600-z6.3a, and MACS0600-z6.4. Observations were done in service mode on the 18th and 19th October 2020 (ID : GN-2020B-Q-903; P.I.: A. Zitrin). We secured 4.5\u00a0h reaching a 1\u03c3 sensitivity of 8.9\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u221219</sup> erg\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup>\u2009cm<sup>\u22122</sup> over the wavelength range of 505 to 980\u00a0nm. We reduced the data using the Gemini <span class=\"small-caps\">iraf</span> package, as recommended by the instrument team. We follow the standard reduction procedure including bias subtraction, flat fielding, wavelength calibration from the illumination of our mask by the CuAr lamp and flux calibration from the white dwarf Wolf 1346.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Interestingly, the continuum of the more compact and brightest image (MACS0600-z6.3a) is visible on the Gemini spectra. We extracted the spectrum in a 1.5\u00d7 seeing diameter aperture and a break is clearly identified between 850 and 900\u00a0nm. To improve the signal, we binned the spectra in the spectral direction with a binning factor of 30 (see Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a>). We determined the spectroscopic redshift by fitting our observed spectra with a stacked spectra coming from 81 LBGs (Jones, Stark &amp; Ellis <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). We searched for the best-fit using a \u03c7<sup>2</sup> minimization technique over a redshift range between <em>z</em> = 0 and <em>z</em> = 8. The best fit is found at <em>z</em><sub>spec</sub> = 6.19<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$^{+0.06}_{-0.16}$|\u2060</span>, consistent with both the photometric redshift and the [C\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]158\u2009<em>\u03bc</em>m emission line detected in the ALMA data. One can also argue that if the break seen in the Gemini data is the Balmer Break at <em>z</em> \u223c 1.1 instead of the Lyman Break at <em>z</em> \u223c 6, we would have detected the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]3727,3729 doublet, which makes the high-redshift identification for this system robust. However, in the case of an extremely dusty <em>z</em> \u223c 1 galaxy, with <em>A<sub>v</sub></em> &gt; 4.5\u2009mag (assuming SFR = 10\u00a0M<sub>\u2299</sub>\u00a0yr<sup>\u22121</sup>), the [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]3727,3729 doublet might be attenuated so as to render its flux below our detection limit. Moreover, after a careful visual inspection of the 2D spectra, no emission line is detected in any of the three images allowing us to place a firm upper limit on the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 luminosity in this <em>z</em> \u223c 6 system at L(Ly\u00a0\u03b1, 2\u03c3) &lt; 2.4\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>42</sup> erg\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup>, corresponding to a rest-frame EW of EW&lt;3.6\u2009\u00c5 assuming a magnification factor of <em>\u03bc</em> = 31. We note that the level of the continuum is consistent with the photometry we measured on <em>HST</em> images (F814W and F105W). While it would be valuable to compare the UV slope inferred from our GMOS spectrum with that indicated photometrically, the limited wavelength range of the form is insufficient for a precise measurement.</p>                        <a id=\"266960842\" scrollto-destination=\"266960842\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/505/4/10.1093_mnras_stab191/1/m_stab191fig5.jpeg?Expires=1639262618&amp;Signature=A4YdKNINkl4XpFUyW0c-M7Qq7Irg6J-T2X-qJjb~8j55OQ1MVQk~PTzi7K7-cum~0O0DqY9NM-wamuPnsdLruabs4fRHiDPNmSpTnCKGSe8cjbYrLrBwv~HblB15vRzTC80A8o2jVgFUQVnXHMiLThIq12sS4kHwePZLver~DubyS~xwotVcE8eFjnBWv1HQjNVuQtf6D~E8cNgFTV8P71TujdC-2i90MhWuvjzCUyoJwepg~hnlIKFy~qFipqGoq7HYQQvotFD1wQlE8GiadgJfR-7Cv4rVvWkyzeRcozxVXqFPglEd8iPRUDdaqDdJD7GfbRWCHuI2SLwKp8Oj9g__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Top: 2D GMOS/Gemini spectrum of MACS0600-z6.3a smoothed with a boxcar of 5\u00a0pixels. (Bottom:) The blue histogram shows the extracted spectrum of MACS0600-z6.3a within a 1.5\u00d7 seeing diameter aperture. The grey histogram displays the \u00b11\u03c3 noise level extracted in a similar size diameter aperture. The red line is the best fit of the Jones et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) spectra to our data which is found at <em>z</em><sub>spec</sub> = 6.19<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$^{+0.06}_{-0.16}$|\u2060</span>, consistent with the redshift measured from [C\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>]158\u2009<em>\u03bc</em>m Fujimoto et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2021</a>).</p></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=266960843 id=\"266960843\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5>5 PHYSICAL PROPERTIES</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We determine the intrinsic (lensing-corrected) physical properties for those two images with a clear dust detection (MACS0600-arc and MACS0600-z6.3b) using <span class=\"small-caps\">magphys</span> (da Cunha, Charlot &amp; Elbaz <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008a</a>), which includes FIR models to fit the dust properties, while we use <span class=\"small-caps\">bagpipes</span> (Carnall et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) to provide constraints for the remaining images. For the <span class=\"small-caps\">bagpipes</span> runs, we assume a constant star formation history (SFH) with a stellar mass ranging from 10<sup>6</sup> to 10<sup>12</sup> M<sub>\u2299</sub>, and an age ranging from 0.0\u00a0Gyr to the age of the Universe at <em>z</em> = 6.07. For each image, we adopt the magnification from the <span class=\"small-caps\">ltm</span> model, based upon the spectroscopic redshift, although as seen in the previous section the magnifications from the three models seem to agree fairly well. Reassuringly, we determine that all images have similar properties. Excluding image MACS0600-z6.3a, which does not seem to contribute significantly to the flux compared to MACS0600-z6.3b, the mean stellar mass is 2.9<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$^{+11.5}_{-2.3}\\times 10^9$|</span>\u00a0M<sub>\u2299</sub>, the mean SFR is 9.7<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$^{+23.0}_{-6.6}$|</span>\u00a0M<sub>\u2299</sub>\u00a0yr<sup>\u22121</sup> and the mean dust mass (computed only from images MACS0600-arc and MACS0600-z6.3b) is 4.8<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$^{+4.5}_{-3.4}$|</span> \u00d7 10<sup>6</sup>\u00a0M<sub>\u2299</sub>, where error bars take into account uncertainties on the magnification factor. The latter is obtained assuming a dust temperature of 30\u00a0K, a dust emissivity of \u03b2 = 2.0 and the mean magnification. Including <em>Herschel</em>/SPIRE 3\u03c3 upper limit (13.9\u00a0mJy/<em>\u03bc</em> at 250\u2009<em>\u03bc</em>m), we can rule out <em>T</em><sub>dust</sub> \u2265 85\u00a0K (Sun et\u00a0al. in preparation). We measure the UV slopes of all images from the best SED fit and find an average \u03b2 = \u22121.66\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.08. We follow the method described in Oesch et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib53\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib53\" data-open=\"bib53\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) to determine the size of this galaxy, taking into account the SE\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">xtractor</span> half-light radius and the <em>Hubble</em> PSF. We apply this method on z6.4, since this image is not blended with other sources. After correcting for magnification, we find an intrinsic size of 0.10\u00a0arcsec corresponding to 0.54<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$^{+0.26}_{-0.14}$|</span> kpc at <em>z</em> \u223c 6.07, in good agreement with previous size estimates at these redshifts (Bouwens et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>; Kawamata et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib39\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib39\" data-open=\"bib39\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>). The individual properties of each image are summarized in Table\u00a0 <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl3\" data-open=\"tbl3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"266960845\" scrollto-destination=\"266960845\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl3\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl3\" data-id=\"tbl3\"><span class=\"label\">Table 3.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Physical properties of all multiple images of MACS0600-z6 computed with <span class=\"small-caps\">magphys</span> (da Cunha et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008a</a>) for sources with dust detection (arc and z6.3b) and <span class=\"small-caps\">bagpipes</span> (Carnall et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) for the remaining. Uncertainties for the <span class=\"small-caps\">ltm</span> model magnification represent the range of values predicted by four other trial LTM models. The central value is obtained by averaging the parameter value of the best-fitting model obtained assuming the mean, min and max magnification value and the error bars included uncertainties on the magnification factor.</p></div> </div><div class=\"table-overflow\"><table><thead><tr><th>Source<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">We can compare the above results for MACS0600-z6 to similar spectroscopically confirmed galaxies at <em>z</em> \u223c 6\u20137 (either a detection or upper limit) in the literature (Kanekar et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib37\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib37\" data-open=\"bib37\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Ouchi et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib56\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib56\" data-open=\"bib56\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Schaerer et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib63\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib63\" data-open=\"bib63\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Knudsen et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib43\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib43\" data-open=\"bib43\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>; Brada\u010d et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>; Marrone et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib52\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib52\" data-open=\"bib52\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>; Smit et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib67\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib67\" data-open=\"bib67\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>). Most of these galaxies have upper limits on their dust content, emphasizing the importance of MACS0600-z6. Despite its modest stellar mass, its dust to stellar mass ratio is somewhat larger than that observed in other <em>z</em> \u223c 6 galaxies (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a>). This implies either that MACS0600-z6 is already a relatively mature system or that its dust production was unusually efficient. We can provide an independent estimate of the stellar age via the amplitude of the Balmer Break (see e.g. Scoville et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib65\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib65\" data-open=\"bib65\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). This requires comparing the fluxes in the F160W and 4.5\u2009<em>\u03bc</em>m bands, since the 3.6\u2009<em>\u03bc</em>m band could be contaminated by strong [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] emission (Labb\u00e9 et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>). Following the methodology discussed in Roberts-Borsani, Ellis &amp; Laporte (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib59\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib59\" data-open=\"bib59\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>), we estimate an age of 200\u00a0\u00b1\u00a0100\u00a0Myr, indicative of a formation redshift of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z\\rm {_{form}}$|</span> = 7.2<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$^{+0.8}_{-0.6}$|\u2060</span>, comparable to values estimated for the other <em>z</em> \u223c 6 galaxies cited above. This relatively young age would suggest that most of the dust detected by ALMA maybe produced by early core-collapse supernovae (SNe) (Gall, Andersen &amp; Hjorth <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>). Assuming a Chabrier (Chabrier <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>) IMF for the production rate of SNe, for the measured dust mass and stellar age, each SN would have produced 0.3<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$^{+0.5}_{-0.2}$|</span> M<sub>\u2299</sub> of dust. Although this estimate is highly uncertain given the uncertain production rate of SNe in early metal-poor galaxies and possible dust destruction and ejection processes in low-mass galaxies at high redshift, it is perhaps somewhat larger than that derived locally (&lt;0.2\u00a0M<sub>\u2299</sub>, see e.g. Cherchneff &amp; Dwek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Gall et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Gomez et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib31\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib31\" data-open=\"bib31\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Indebetouw et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib34\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib34\" data-open=\"bib34\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). Recent chemical evolution models predict dust-to-mass ratios similar to that observed for MACS0600-z6 could be achieved in \u2264200\u00a0Myr (Calura et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). Even higher values have also been observed recently in MAMBO-9 (Casey et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>), an intensely star-forming submm galaxy whose properties are otherwise quite distinct from those of MACS0600-z6. Applying the same method, MAMBO-9 may be even more efficient to produce dust, but the different nature of these two objects makes the comparison of their dust production efficiency difficult.</p>                        <a id=\"266960847\" scrollto-destination=\"266960847\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig6\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 6.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/505/4/10.1093_mnras_stab191/1/m_stab191fig6.jpeg?Expires=1639262618&amp;Signature=Lal0EL-yydiuE-rK62mxk3tVvS~fOUeZU5fddy0oiBtnL7jtMNM9lEd8cy9RqKtFRM6fQ3GogJTvmlbQr8Y4gy3NQuPSIhx4oMtpVXyO3TARAjdhzXUKjAldC8LH0iCWkqKj29d3ezdEWDKyaL8dd2t98Skpk~tl~NQB1c5xPxfWcF-Up0XhdTESGRN41RTfFT95qCflxyEFPx18UucBbNNmvmMopT1ARFrVg6DsTEKL1B0nvNhsoXbCR9L30IXOfcNpC-RPOByhkL5ugchmrEZuvMKM331Qa0CTQX5k9pvLt1Xx0As0dJxJBNkqiX0QaCaTM1f0mVyLoEFORnRAOw__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Dust to stellar mass ratio as a function of the stellar mass. The ratio for MACS0600-z6 is fairly high for its redshift, indicating either that it is relatively old or that its dust production was unusually efficient. The green circle shows the position of MAMBO-9, a sub-mm galaxy with an extreme dust to stellar mass ratio at <em>z</em> = 5.9 (Casey et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>); the distinct natures of these two galaxies (sub-mm versus LBG) makes a comparison of their dust production efficiency difficult. The red dashed arrow shows the direction in parameter space that the LBG would move when taking into account high dust temperature (<em>T</em> = 85\u00a0K) and uncertainties on the magnification..</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The ratio between the IR and UV luminosity, often referred to as IRX = <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\log (L_{IR}/\\rm {L_{UV}}$|\u2060</span>), can be compared to the UV continuum slope \u03b2 to offer insight into the dust extinction law at early cosmic epochs. Bouwens et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>) found that <em>z</em> &gt; 4 galaxies with log\u2009[<em>M</em><sub>\u22c6</sub> &lt;9.75] (comparable to MACS0600-z6) may have extinction laws that deviate from both the Calzetti et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>) and SMC relations, in the sense of having lower IRX values. They argued that a higher dust temperature may explain this difference. Although there is some evidence for higher dust temperatures at <em>z</em> \u2265 8 (Behrens et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>; Laporte et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib49\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib49\" data-open=\"bib49\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>; Bakx et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>), there is currently no strong evidence for evolution at <em>z</em> \u223c 6 (e.g. Schreiber et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib64\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib64\" data-open=\"bib64\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>; Faisst et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>). Assuming a dust temperature of 35K to estimate the IR luminosity of MACS0600-z6 and the other <em>z</em> \u223c 6 galaxies, Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig7\" data-open=\"fig7\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">7</a> shows that most <em>z</em> \u223c 6 galaxies follow the Calzetti law.</p>                        <a id=\"266960849\" scrollto-destination=\"266960849\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig7\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 7.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/505/4/10.1093_mnras_stab191/1/m_stab191fig7.jpeg?Expires=1639262618&amp;Signature=dne6DD9tPJxW-~ornMcknys7U-hQedpL-fE7dDsXVssDSbv8uPWHBnhDPnhKQ0JdG~GQrLIrqIP8Qqy0mqKhpCsuhQ5VOR-xIhI-3ZI-dLxmYhrxYZLG4I1KlTGW2nuMmveQrZPt73Ze1as4OXal8qT3y~K1ZrbLRUBkf3Giwc5SWmyd31rFu5xutOjF06qMCXCc1TdBRmdKZb7xA0yy~EMIVPS7EuFDpqfYqOsmWT9xEXORlvw1LCKh1Z8NWljO6QB~QJpMnY03SshUh9N9nO2oqr0~sPcpb4nlUR4wybWVUi2S0c-7mKMmAtAQCo226dUlhB2kllT~W5kckBU8Eg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The IR/UV luminosity ratio IRX as a function of the UV slope \u03b2. Black points represent galaxies at z \u2265 7, blue points are z \u223c 6 galaxies and the red circle shows MACS0600-z6. All values are computed assuming a dust temperature of 35\u00a0K. The expected trend assuming the Calzetti et\u00a0al. (2000) and SMC laws are shown.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab191fig7.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/266960849/stab191fig7.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab191fig7.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"266960849\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/505/4/10.1093_mnras_stab191/1/stab191fig7.jpeg?Expires=1639262618&Signature=WnavTMIJh3McYlDMSzWy4vCKCDyIRvaXK75K5ksijtohAo5eHampxluXYwIiOZbaaQE2FTGCPfQXuNfNqcqs3Lz1rNrG1hvhPrsFOD-AUO4QFF~mb4mQEWLPsB3J77fypKnJgZw5zc2-C~i8aXsN6mE32luqs-FzlWEXpXYtL~ybBStL0tYAQAQULnfzFohox7ZoK52tB~Umb2HvDOKubw11X8-pEVyi2Uqj8v~3t1EYPYVljWoj084z5lpzDWq8gZG8eGqGdQsnRmfWJISHxRk~04Ozb1WNPHZ4gAQuaG9Cf0jiDguDV2CybjRIgOKpEg2o6dWoz4NeJkQAtYJwjg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=266960849&ar=6122579&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab191fig7.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">The IR/UV luminosity ratio IRX as a function of the UV slope \u03b2. (2000) and SMC laws are shown.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab191fig7.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/266960849/stab191fig7.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab191fig7.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"266960849\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/505/4/10.1093_mnras_stab191/1/stab191fig7.jpeg?Expires=1639262618&Signature=WnavTMIJh3McYlDMSzWy4vCKCDyIRvaXK75K5ksijtohAo5eHampxluXYwIiOZbaaQE2FTGCPfQXuNfNqcqs3Lz1rNrG1hvhPrsFOD-AUO4QFF~mb4mQEWLPsB3J77fypKnJgZw5zc2-C~i8aXsN6mE32luqs-FzlWEXpXYtL~ybBStL0tYAQAQULnfzFohox7ZoK52tB~Umb2HvDOKubw11X8-pEVyi2Uqj8v~3t1EYPYVljWoj084z5lpzDWq8gZG8eGqGdQsnRmfWJISHxRk~04Ozb1WNPHZ4gAQuaG9Cf0jiDguDV2CybjRIgOKpEg2o6dWoz4NeJkQAtYJwjg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=266960849&ar=6122579&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab191fig7.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">The IR/UV luminosity ratio IRX as a function of the UV slope \u03b2. Black points represent galaxies at <em>z</em> \u2265 7, blue points are <em>z</em> \u223c 6 galaxies and the red circle shows MACS0600-z6. All values are computed assuming a dust temperature of 35\u00a0K. The expected trend assuming the Calzetti et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>) and SMC laws are shown.</p></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=266960850 id=\"266960850\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec6>6 DISCUSSION AND CONCLUSION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Recent studies have suggested that the dust temperature may be higher at high-redshift than what is measured at lower redshift. Obtaining an accurate measurement of the dust temperature in high-redshift galaxies requires to constrain the red slope and the peak of the FIR emission (see fig. 1 of da Cunha, Charlot &amp; Elbaz <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008b</a>). The evolution of the dust temperature with redshift can be studied at intermediate redshift combining data from <em>Herschel</em> and ALMA. Schreiber et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib64\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib64\" data-open=\"bib64\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) demonstrate that the dust temperature goes from 25K at <em>z</em> \u22641 up to 40\u00a0K at <em>z</em> \u223c 5. At <em>z</em> \u2265 7, few sources have been observed at multiple sub-mm wavelengths (Watson et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib69\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib69\" data-open=\"bib69\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Knudsen et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib44\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib44\" data-open=\"bib44\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>; Laporte et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib48\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib48\" data-open=\"bib48\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017b</a>; Laporte et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib49\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib49\" data-open=\"bib49\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>; Tamura et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib68\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib68\" data-open=\"bib68\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>; Bakx et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>). They all estimate a dust temperature at <em>z</em> \u2265 7 above the \u2018standard\u2019 value of 30\u00a0K observed at low-redshift, but deeper data at \u03bb \u2265 1\u00a0mm are needed. Recent theoretical models suggest that the dust temperature in <em>z</em> \u2265 5 galaxies is <em>T</em><sub>dust</sub> = 45\u00a0K for 0.1\u2009<em>\u03bc</em>m grain, and could reach as high temperature as <em>T</em><sub>dust</sub> \u2265 60\u00a0K for smaller grains (Ferrara et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). In view of this, we explore whether a higher dust temperature would change our conclusions. For a temperature of 85\u00a0K, the estimated dust mass would decrease to <em>M</em><sub>dust</sub> = 6.3<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$^{+1.6}_{3.6}$|</span> \u00d7 10<sup>6</sup>\u00a0M<sub>\u2299</sub>, and its dust-to-stellar mass ratio will be comparable to previous findings at high redshift. Further ALMA observations at longer wavelength (e.g. in band 5) are needed to constrain the dust temperature and to refine our dust mass estimates. Moreover, adopting a higher dust temperature to study the IRX\u2013\u03b2<sub>uv</sub> relation confirms our conclusion on the dust law preferred by our object, since an increase in dust temperature will increase the dust luminosity without changing the UV luminosity, and will therefore tend to higher IRX, consistent with the Calzetti law.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Such intrinsically faint sources (<em>M</em><sub>uv</sub> = \u221219.9\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.15) emitting light during the Epoch of Reionization are considered to be dominant contributors to the cosmic reionisation of hydrogen (e.g. Atek et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Bouwens et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). This strongly lensed system has therefore the capabilities of testing this hypothesis. Recent studies of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 emission line (either from LBG or LAE) using MUSE/VLT (e.g. de La Vieuville et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>; de La Vieuville et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>) or the Hyper Suprime-Cam/Subaru (e.g. Konno et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib45\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib45\" data-open=\"bib45\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) show that the luminosity of Ly\u00a0\u03b1 at <em>z</em> \u2265 5.5 ranges from 10<sup>40</sup> to 10<sup>43.8</sup> erg\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup>. The Ly\u00a0\u03b1 properties in MACS0600-z6 (L(2\u03c3) &lt;2.4\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>42</sup> erg\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup> and EW<sub>RF</sub> &lt; 3.6 \u00c5) are therefore not particularly exceptional and comparable in luminosity and Ly\u00a0\u03b1 EW to the bulk of the galaxy population at <em>z</em> \u223c 6.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We report the discovery of a <em>z</em> = 6.07 dusty galaxy strongly lensed by the cluster MACS0600.1-2007 comprising five multiple images. We used three different mass models for the cluster, showing good agreement between predicted magnification factors and observed flux ratio between the five images of this galaxy. The physical properties we deduced from a detailed SED analysis show that this galaxy has a stellar mass of \u223c10<sup>9</sup><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm {M_{\\odot }}$|\u2060</span>, a dust mass of \u223c10<sup>6</sup><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm {M_{\\odot }}$|\u2060</span>, respectively, a small star formation rate (<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">\u2060|$\\lt 10\\rm {M_{\\odot }\\, yr^{-1}}$|\u2060</span>) and a size (\u223c0.5\u00a0kpc) consistent with previous observations. We estimate the dust production rate in this galaxy and conclude that it seems higher than what has been observed in <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm {z\\le 5}$|</span> galaxies. Further sub-mm observations, as provided by ALMA, are crucial to improve the estimate of the dust content of this galaxy.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=266960854 id=\"266960854\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title js-splitscreen-backacknowledgements-title\" data-legacy-id=ack1>ACKNOWLEDGEMENTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We thank the referee for providing useful comments which improved the quality of this paper, the Gemini Helpdesk team for their help with the reduction of Gemini data and Ian Smail for useful comments on this manuscript.
