</div>\r\n\r\n\r\n</body>\r\n</html>\r\n\r\n", "Status": "Complete", "Action": "Scanned all subtables", "Table captions or footers": {"Overview": " class=\"chapter-para\">We can compare the above results for MACS0600-z6 to similar spectroscopically confirmed galaxies at <em>z</em> \u223c 6\u20137 (either a detection or upper limit) in the literature (Kanekar et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib37\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib37\" data-open=\"bib37\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Ouchi et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib56\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib56\" data-open=\"bib56\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Schaerer et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib63\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib63\" data-open=\"bib63\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Knudsen et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib43\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib43\" data-open=\"bib43\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>; Brada\u010d et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>; Marrone et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib52\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib52\" data-open=\"bib52\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>; Smit et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib67\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib67\" data-open=\"bib67\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>). Most of these galaxies have upper limits on their dust content, emphasizing the importance of MACS0600-z6. Despite its modest stellar mass, its dust to stellar mass ratio is somewhat larger than that observed in other <em>z</em> \u223c 6 galaxies (Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a>). This implies either that MACS0600-z6 is already a relatively mature system or that its dust production was unusually efficient. We can provide an independent estimate of the stellar age via the amplitude of the Balmer Break (see e.g. Scoville et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib65\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib65\" data-open=\"bib65\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). This requires comparing the fluxes in the F160W and 4.5\u2009<em>\u03bc</em>m bands, since the 3.6\u2009<em>\u03bc</em>m band could be contaminated by strong [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] emission (Labb\u00e9 et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>). Following the methodology discussed in Roberts-Borsani, Ellis &amp; Laporte (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib59\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib59\" data-open=\"bib59\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>), we estimate an age of 200\u00a0\u00b1\u00a0100\u00a0Myr, indicative of a formation redshift of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$z\\rm {_{form}}$|</span> = 7.2<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$^{+0.8}_{-0.6}$|\u2060</span>, comparable to values estimated for the other <em>z</em> \u223c 6 galaxies cited above. This relatively young age would suggest that most of the dust detected by ALMA maybe produced by early core-collapse supernovae (SNe) (Gall, Andersen &amp; Hjorth <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>). Assuming a Chabrier (Chabrier <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>) IMF for the production rate of SNe, for the measured dust mass and stellar age, each SN would have produced 0.3<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$^{+0.5}_{-0.2}$|</span> M<sub>\u2299</sub> of dust. Although this estimate is highly uncertain given the uncertain production rate of SNe in early metal-poor galaxies and possible dust destruction and ejection processes in low-mass galaxies at high redshift, it is perhaps somewhat larger than that derived locally (&lt;0.2\u00a0M<sub>\u2299</sub>, see e.g. Cherchneff &amp; Dwek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Gall et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Gomez et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib31\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib31\" data-open=\"bib31\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Indebetouw et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib34\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib34\" data-open=\"bib34\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). Recent chemical evolution models predict dust-to-mass ratios similar to that observed for MACS0600-z6 could be achieved in \u2264200\u00a0Myr (Calura et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). Even higher values have also been observed recently in MAMBO-9 (Casey et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>), an intensely star-forming submm galaxy whose properties are otherwise quite distinct from those of MACS0600-z6. Applying the same method, MAMBO-9 may be even more efficient to produce dust, but the different nature of these two objects makes the comparison of their dust production efficiency difficult."},
